/// Provider for `query mir_borrowck`. Similar to `typeck`, this must\n115: /// only be called for typeck roots which will then borrowck all\n116: /// nested bodies as well.\n117: fn mir_borrowck(\n118:     tcx: TyCtxt<'_>,\n119:     def: LocalDefId,\n120: ) -> Result<&FxIndexMap<LocalDefId, ty::DefinitionSiteHiddenType<'_>>, ErrorGuaranteed> {\n121:     assert!(!tcx.is_typeck_child(def.to_def_id()));\n122:     let (input_body, _) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n123:     debug!(\"run query mir_borrowck: {}\", tcx.def_path_str(def));\n124: \n125:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n126:     if let Some(guar) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n127:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of tainted body\");\n128:         Err(guar)\n129:     } else if input_body.should_skip() {\n130:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of injected body\");\n131:         let opaque_types = Default::default();\n132:         Ok(tcx.arena.alloc(opaque_types))\n133:     } else {\n134:         let mut root_cx = BorrowCheckRootCtxt::new(tcx, def, None);\n135:         root_cx.do_mir_borrowck();\n136:         root_cx.finalize()\n137:     }\n138: }\n139: \n140: /// Data propagated to the typeck parent by nested items.\n141: /// This should always be empty for the typeck root.\n142: #[derive(Debug)]\n143: struct PropagatedBorrowCheckResults<'tcx> {\n144:     closure_requirements: Option<ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx>>,\n145:     used_mut_upvars: SmallVec<[FieldIdx; 8]>,\n146: }\n147: \n148: type DeferredClosureRequirements<'tcx> = Vec<(LocalDefId, ty::GenericArgsRef<'tcx>, Locations)>;\n149: \n150: /// After we borrow check a closure, we are left with various\n151: /// requirements that we have inferred between the free regions that\n152: /// appear in the closure's signature or on its field types. These\n153: /// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\n154: /// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\n155: ///\n156: /// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n237:     /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n238:     Region(ty::RegionVid),\n239: }\n240: \n241: /// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n242: ///\n243: /// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n244: /// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n245: /// a query response.\n246: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n247: pub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n248:     inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n249: }\n250: // DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n251: // type is not recognized as a binder for late-bound region.\n252: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeVisitable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n253: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeFoldable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n254: \n255: impl<'tcx> ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n256:     /// All regions of `ty` must be of kind `ReVar` and must represent\n257:     /// universal regions *external* to the closure.\n258:     pub fn bind(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n259:         let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n260:             ty::ReVar(vid) => {\n261:                 let br = ty::BoundRegion {\n262:                     var: ty::BoundVar::from_usize(vid.index()),\n263:                     kind: ty::BoundRegionKind::Anon,\n264:                 };\n265:                 ty::Region::new_bound(tcx, depth, br)\n266:             }\n267:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region in ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy: {r:?}\"),\n268:         });\n269: \n270:         Self { inner }\n271:     }\n272: \n273:     pub fn instantiate(\n274:         self,\n275:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n276:         mut map: impl FnMut(ty::RegionVid) -> ty::Region<'tcx>,\n277:     ) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n278:         fold_regions(tcx, self.inner, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n279:             ty::ReBound(ty::BoundVarIndexKind::Bound(debruijn), br) => {\n280:                 debug_assert_eq!(debruijn, depth);\n281:                 map(ty::RegionVid::from_usize(br.var.index()))\n282:             }\n283:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region {r:?}\"),\n284:         })\n285:     }\n286: }\n287: \n288: struct CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n289:     infcx: This initializes the relevant data structures\n308: /// and then type checks the MIR body.\n309: fn borrowck_collect_region_constraints<'tcx>(\n310:     root_cx: &mut BorrowCheckRootCtxt<'tcx>,\n311:     def: LocalDefId,\n312: ) -> CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n313:     let tcx = root_cx.tcx;\n314:     let infcx = BorrowckInferCtxt::new(tcx, def, root_cx.root_def_id());\n315:     let (input_body, promoted) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n316:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n317:     let input_promoted: &IndexSlice<_, _> = &promoted.borrow();\n318:     if let Some(e) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n319:         infcx.set_tainted_by_errors(e);\n320:         root_cx.set_tainted_by_errors(e);\n321:     }\n322: \n323:     // Replace all regions with fresh inference variables. This\n324:     // requires first making our own copy of the MIR. This copy will\n325:     // be modified (in place) to contain non-lexical lifetimes. It\n326:     // will have a lifetime tied to the inference context.\n327:     let mut body_owned = input_body.clone();\n328:     let mut promoted = input_promoted.to_owned();\n329:     let .map(|(borrows, uninits, ever_inits)| BorrowckDomain { borrows, uninits, ever_inits })\n633:             .collect();\n634: \n635:     Results { analysis, entry_states }\n636: }\n637: \n638: pub(crate) \n781: // Check that:\n782: // 1. assignments are always made to mutable locations (FIXME: does that still really go here?)\n783: // 2. loans made in overlapping scopes do not conflict\n784: // 3. assignments do not affect things loaned out as immutable\n785: // 4. moves do not affect things loaned out in any way\n786: impl<'a, 'tcx> ResultsVisitor<'tcx, Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>> for MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n787:     fn visit_after_early_statement_effect(\n788:         &mut self,\n789:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n790:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n791:         stmt: &Statement<'tcx>,\n792:         location: Location,\n793:     ) {\n794:         debug!(\"MirBorrowckCtxt::process_statement({:?}, {:?}): {:?}\", location, stmt, state);\n795:         let span = stmt.source_info.span;\n796: \n797:         self.check_activations(location, span, state);\n798: \n799:         match &stmt.kind {\n800:             StatementKind::Assign(box (lhs, rhs)) => {\n801:                 self.consume_rvalue(location, (rhs, span), state);\n802: \n803:                 self.mutate_place(location, (*lhs, span), Shallow(None), state);\n804:             }\n805:             StatementKind::FakeRead(box (_, place)) => {\n806:                 // Read for match doesn't access any memory and is used to\n807:                 // assert that a place is safe and live. So we don't have to\n808:                 // do any checks here.\n809:                 //\n810:                 // FIXME: Remove check that the place is initialized. This is\n811:                 // needed for now because matches don't have never patterns yet.\n812:                 // So this is the only place we prevent\n813:                 //      let x:          InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n819:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n820:                     state,\n821:                 );\n822:             }\n823:             StatementKind::Intrinsic(box kind) => match kind {\n824:                 NonDivergingIntrinsic::Assume(op) => {\n825:                     self.consume_operand(location, (op, span), state);\n826:                 }\n827:                 NonDivergingIntrinsic::CopyNonOverlapping(..) => span_bug!(\n828:                     span,\n829:                     \"Unexpected CopyNonOverlapping, should only appear after lower_intrinsics\",\n830:                 )\n831:             }\n832:             // Only relevant for mir typeck\n833:             StatementKind::AscribeUserType(..)\n834:             // {}\n841:             // This does not affect borrowck\n842:             StatementKind::BackwardIncompatibleDropHint { place, reason: BackwardIncompatibleDropReason::Edition2024 } => {\n843:                 self.check_backward_incompatible_drop(location, **place, state);\n844:             }\n845:             StatementKind::StorageDead(local) => {\n846:                 self.access_place(\n847: LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n851:                     state,\n852:                 );\n853:             }\n854:             StatementKind::Nop\n855:             | StatementKind::Retag { .. }\n856:             | StatementKind::SetDiscriminant { .. } => {\n857:                 bug!(\"Statement not allowed in this MIR phase\")\n858:             }\n859:         }\n860:     }\n861: \n862:     fn loc: Location,\n868:     ) {\n869:         debug!(\"MirBorrowckCtxt::process_terminator({:?}, {:?}): {:?}\", loc, term, state);\n870:         let span = term.source_info.span;\n871: \n872:         self.check_activations(loc, span, state);\n873: \n874:         match &term.kind {\n875:             TerminatorKind::SwitchInt { discr, targets: _ } => {\n876:                 self.consume_operand(loc,           loc: {:?} term: {:?} place: {:?} span: {:?}\",\n889:                     loc, term, place, span\n890:                 );\n891: \n892:                 let write_kind =\n893:                (AccessDepth::Drop, Write(write_kind)),\n898:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n899:                     state,\n900:                 );\n901:             }\n902:             TerminatorKind::Call {\n903:                 func,\n904:                 args,\n905:                 destination,\n906:                 target: _,\n907:                 unwind: _,\n908:                 call_source: _,\n909:                 fn_span: _,\n910:             } => {\n911:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (func, span), state);\n912:                 for arg in args {\n913:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (&arg.node, arg.span), state);\n914:                 }\n915:                 self.mutate_place(loc, (*destination, span), Deep, state);\n916:             }\n917:             TerminatorKind::TailCall { func, args, fn_span: _ } => {\n918:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (func, span), state);\n919:                 for arg in args {\n920:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (&arg.node, arg.span), state);\n921:                 }\n922:             }\n923:             TerminatorKind::Assert { cond, expected: _, msg, target: _, unwind: _ self.consume_operand(loc, (len, span), state);\n927:                     self.consume_operand(loc, (index, span), state);\n928:                 }\n929:             }\n930: \n931:             TerminatorKind::Yield { value, resume: _, resume_arg, drop: _ } => {\n932:                 self.consume_operand(loc, (value, span), state);\n933:                 self.mutate_place(loc, (*resume_arg, visit_after_primary_terminator_effect(\n983:         &mut self,\n984:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n985:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n986:         term: &Terminator<'tcx>,\n987:              let borrow = &self.borrow_set[i];\n997:                         self.check_for_local_borrow(borrow, span);\n998:                     }\n999:                 }\n1000:             }\n1001: {\n1006:                 match self.borrow_set.locals_state_at_exit() {\n1007:                     LocalsStateAtExit::AllAreInvalidated => {\n1008:                         // Returning from the              }\n1016:                     }\n1017:                     // If we do not implicitly invalidate all locals on exit,\n1018:                     // we check for conflicts when dropping or moving this local.\n1019:                     LocalsStateAtExit::SomeAreInvalidated { has_storage_dead_or_moved: _ } => {}\n1020:                 }\n1021:             }\n1022: \n1023: }\n1035: }\n1036: \n1037: use self::AccessDepth::{Deep, Shallow};\n1038: use self::ReadOrWrite::{Activation, Read, Reservation, Write};\n1039: \n1040: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1041: enum ArtificialField {\n1042:     ArrayLength,\n1043:     FakeBorrow,\n1044: }\n1045: \n1046: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1047: enum AccessDepth {\n1048:     /// From the RFC: \"A *shallow* access means that the immediate\n1049:     /// fields reached at P are accessed, but references or pointers\n1050:     /// found within are not dereferenced. Right now, the only access\n1051:     /// that is shallow is an assignment like `x = ...;`, which would\n1052:     /// be a *shallow write* of `x`.\"\n1053:     Shallow(Option<ArtificialField>),\n1054: \n1055:     /// From the RFC: \"A *deep* access means that all data reachable\n1056:     /// through the given place may be invalidated or accesses by\n1057:     /// this action.\"\n1058:     Deep,\n1059: \n1060:     /// Access is Deep only when there is a Drop implementation that\n1061:     /// can reach the data behind the reference.\n1062:     Drop,\n1063: }\n1064: \n1065: /// Kind of access to a value: read or write\n1066: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1067: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1068: enum ReadOrWrite {\n1069:     /// From the RFC: \"A *read* means that the existing data may be\n1070:     /// read, but will not be changed.\"\n1071:     Read(ReadKind),\n1072: \n1073:     /// From the RFC: \"A Kind of read access to a value\n1086: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1087: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1088: enum ReadKind {\n1089:     Borrow(BorrowKind),\n1090: StorageDeadOrDrop,\n1098:     Replace,\n1099:     MutableBorrow(BorrowKind),\n1100:     Mutate,\n1101:     Move,\n1102: }\n1103: \n1104: /// When checking permissions for a place access, this flag is \n1168: impl<'a, 'tcx> MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n1169:     fn body(&self) -> &'a Body<'tcx> {\n1170:         self.body\n1171:     }\n1172: \n1173:     /// Checks an access to the given place to ) -> Cow<'s, MixedBitSet<BorrowIndex>> {\n1232:         if let Some(polonius) = &self.polonius_output {\n1233:             // Use polonius output if it has been enabled.\n1234:             let   ) -> bool {\n1254:         let mut error_reported = false;\n1255: \n1256:         let borrows_in_scope = self.borrows_in_scope(location, state);\n1257: \n1258:      }\n1370:             },\n1371:         );\n1372: \n1373:         error_reported\n1374:     }\n1375: \n1376:     /// Through #123739, `BackwardIncompatibleDropHint`s (BIDs) are introduced.\n1377:     /// We would like to emit lints whether borrow checking fails at these future drop locations.\n1378:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1379:     fn check_backward_incompatible_drop(\n1380:         &mut self,\n1381:         location: Location,\n1382:         place: Place<'tcx>,\n1383:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1384:     ) {\n1385: {\n1390:             AccessDepth::Drop\n1391:         } else {\n1392:             AccessDepth::Shallow(None)\n1393:         };\n1394: \n1395:         let borrows_in_scope = self.borrows_in_scope(location, state);\n1396: \n1397:         // This is a very simplified version of `Self::check_access_for_conflict`.\n1398:         // We are here checking on BIDs and specifically still-live borrows of data involving the BIDs.\n1399:         each_borrow_involving_path(\n1400:             self,\n1401:             self.infcx.tcx,\n1402:             self.body,\n1403:             (sd, place),\n1404:             self.borrow_set,\n1405:             |borrow_index| borrows_in_scope.contains(borrow_index),\n1406:             |this, _borrow_index, borrow| {\n1407:                 if matches!(borrow.kind, BorrowKind::Fake(_)) {\n1408:                     return ControlFlow::Continue(());\n1409:                 }\n1410:                 let borrowed = this.retrieve_borrow_spans(borrow).var_or_use_path_span();\n1411:                 let explain = this.explain_why_borrow_contains_point(\n1412:                     location,\n1413:                     borrow,\n1414:                     Some((WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop, place)),\n1415:                 );\n1416:                 this.infcx.tcx.node_span_lint(\n1417:                     TAIL_EXPR_DROP_ORDER,\n1418:                     CRATE_HIR_ID,\n1419:                     borrowed,\n1420:                     |diag| {\n1421:                         session_diagnostics::TailExprDropOrder { borrowed }.decorate_lint(diag);\n1422:                         explain.add_explanation_to_diagnostic(&this, diag, \"\", None, None);\n1423:                     },\n1424:                 );\n1425:                 // We may stop at the first case\n1426:                 ControlFlow::Break(())\n1427:             },\n1428:         );\n1429:     }\n1430: \n1431:     fn mutate_place(\n1432:         &mut self,\n1433:         location: Location,\n1434:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1435:         kind: AccessDepth,\n1436:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1437:     ) {\n1438:         // Write of P[i] or *P requires P init'd.\n1439:         self.check_if_assigned_path_is_moved(location, place_span, state);\n1440: \n1441:         self.access_place(\n1442:             location,\n1443:             place_span,\n1444:             (kind, Write(WriteKind::Mutate)),\n1445:             LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1446:             state,\n1447:         );\n1448:     }\n1449: \n1450:     fn consume_rvalue(\n1451:         &mut self,\n1452:         location: Location,\n1453:         (rvalue, span): (&Rvalue<'tcx>, Span),\n1454:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1455:     ) {\n1456:         match rvalue {\n1457:             &Rvalue::Ref(_ /*rgn*/, bk, place) => {\n1458:                 let access_kind = match bk {\n1459:                     BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow) => {\n1460:                         (Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::FakeBorrow)), Read(ReadKind::Borrow(bk)))\n1461:                     }\n1462:                     BorrowKind::Shared | BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Deep) => {\n1463:                         (Deep, Read(ReadKind::Borrow(bk)))\n1464:                     }\n1465:                     BorrowKind::Mut { .. } => {\n1466:                         let wk = WriteKind::MutableBorrow(bk);\n1467:                         if bk.allows_two_phase_borrow() {\n1468:                             (Deep, Reservation(wk))\n1469:                         } else {\n1470:                             (Deep, Write(wk))\n1471:                         }\n1472:                     }\n1473:                 };\n1474: \n1475:                 self.access_place(\n1476:                     location,\n1477:                     (place, span),\n1478:                     access_kind,\n1479:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1480:                     state,\n1481:                 );\n1482: \n1483:                 let action = if bk == BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow) {\n1484:                     InitializationRequiringAction::MatchOn\n1485:                 } else {\n1486:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Borrow\n1487:                 };\n1488: \n1489:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1490:                     location,\n1491:                     action,\n1492:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1493:                     state,\n1494:                 );\n1495:             }\n1496: \n1497:             &Rvalue::RawPtr(kind, place) => {\n1498:                 let access_kind = match kind {\n1499:                     RawPtrKind::Mut => (\n1500:                         Deep,\n1501:                         Write(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Mut {\n1502:                             kind: MutBorrowKind::Default,\n1503:                         })),\n1504:                     ),\n1505:                     RawPtrKind::Const => (Deep, Read(ReadKind::Borrow(BorrowKind::Shared))),\n1506:                     RawPtrKind::FakeForPtrMetadata => {\n1507:                         (Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)), Read(ReadKind::Copy))\n1508:                     }\n1509:                 };\n1510: \n1511:                 self.access_place(\n1512:                     location,\n1513:                     (place, span),\n1514:                     access_kind,\n1515:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1516:                     state,\n1517:                 );\n1518: \n1519:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1520:                     location,\n1521:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Borrow,\n1522:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1523:                     state,\n1524:                 );\n1525:             }\n1526: \n1527:             Rvalue::ThreadLocalRef(_) => {}\n1528: \n1529:             Rvalue::Use(operand)\n1530:             | Rvalue::Repeat(operand, _)\n1531:             | Rvalue::UnaryOp(_ /*un_op*/, operand)\n1532:             | Rvalue::Cast(_ /*cast_kind*/, operand, _ /*ty*/)\n1533:             | Rvalue::ShallowInitBox(operand, _ /*ty*/) => {\n1534:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand, span), state)\n1535:             }\n1536: \n1537:             &Rvalue::Discriminant(place) => {\n1538:                 let af = match *rvalue {\n1539:                     Rvalue::Discriminant(..) => None,\n1540:                     _ => unreachable!(),\n1541:                 };\n1542:                 self.access_place(\n1543:                     location,\n1544:                     (place, span),\n1545:                     (Shallow(af), Read(ReadKind::Copy)),\n1546:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1547:                     state,\n1548:                 );\n1549:                 self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n1550:                     location,\n1551:                     InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n1552:                     (place.as_ref(), span),\n1553:                     state,\n1554:                 );\n1555:             }\n1556: \n1557:             Rvalue::BinaryOp(_bin_op, box (operand1, operand2)) => {\n1558:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand1, span), state);\n1559:                 self.consume_operand(location, (operand2, span), state);\n1560:             }\n1561: \n1562:             Rvalue::NullaryOp(_op) => {\n1563:                 // nullary ops take no dynamic input; no borrowck effect.\n1564:             }\n1565: \n1566:             Rvalue::Aggregate(aggregate_kind, operands) => {\n1567:                 // We need to report back the list of mutable upvars that were\n1568:                 // moved into the closure and subsequently used by the closure,\n1569:                 // in order to populate our used_mut set.\n1570:                 match **aggregate_kind {\n1571:                     AggregateKind::Closure(def_id, _)\n1572:                     | AggregateKind::CoroutineClosure(def_id, _)\n1573:                     | AggregateKind::Coroutine(def_id, _) => {\n1574:                         let def_id = def_id.expect_local();\n1575:                         let used_mut_upvars = self.root_cx.used_mut_upvars(def_id);\n1576:                         debug!(\"{:?} used_mut_upvars={:?}\", def_id, used_mut_upvars);\n1577:                         // FIXME: We're cloning the `SmallVec` here to avoid borrowing `root_cx`\n1578:                         // when calling `propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar`. This should ideally\n1579:                         // be unnecessary.\n1580:                         for field in used_mut_upvars.clone() {\n1581:                             self.propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar(&operands[field]);\n1582:                         }\n1583:                     }\n1584:                     AggregateKind::Adt(..)\n1585:                     | AggregateKind::Array(..)\n1586:                     | AggregateKind::Tuple { .. }\n1587:                     | AggregateKind::RawPtr(..) => (),\n1588:                 }\n1589: \n1590:                 for operand in operands {\n1591:                     self.consume_operand(location, (operand, span), state);\n1592:                 }\n1593:             }\n1594: \n1595:             Rvalue::WrapUnsafeBinder(op, _) => {\n1596:                 self.consume_operand(location, (op, span), state);\n1597:             }\n1598: \n1599:             Rvalue::CopyForDeref(_) => bug!(\"`CopyForDeref` in borrowck\"),\n1600:         }\n1601:     }\n1602: \n1603:     fn propagate_closure_used_mut_upvar(&mut self, operand: &Operand<'tcx>) {\n1604:         let propagate_closure_used_mut_place = |this: &mut Self, place: Place<'tcx>| {\n1605:             // We have three possibilities here:\n1606:             // a. We are modifying something through a mut-ref\n1607:             // b. We are modifying something that is local to our parent\n1608:             // c. Current body is a nested closure, and we are modifying path starting from\n1609:             //    a Place captured by our parent closure.\n1610: \n1611:             // Handle (c), the path being modified is exactly the path captured by our parent\n1612:             if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place.as_ref()) {\n1613:                 this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1614:                 return;\n1615:             }\n1616: \n1617:             for (place_ref, proj) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n1618:                 // Handle (a)\n1619:                 if proj == ProjectionElem::Deref {\n1620:                     match place_ref.ty(this.body(), this.infcx.tcx).ty.kind() {\n1621:                         // We aren't modifying a variable directly\n1622:                         ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut) => return,\n1623: \n1624:                         _ => {}\n1625:                     }\n1626:                 }\n1627: \n1628:                 // Handle (c)\n1629:                 if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place_ref) {\n1630:                     this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1631:                     return;\n1632:                 }\n1633:             }\n1634: \n1635:             // Handle(b)\n1636:             this.used_mut.insert(place.local);\n1637:         };\n1638: \n1639:         // This relies on the current way that by-value\n1640:         // captures of a closure are copied/moved directly\n1641:         // when generating MIR.\n1642:         match *operand {\n1643:             Operand::Move(place) | Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1644:                 match place.as_local() {\n1645:                     Some(local) if !self.body.local_decls[local].is_user_variable() => {\n1646:                         if self.body.local_decls[local].ty.is_mutable_ptr() {\n1647:                             // The variable will be marked as mutable by the borrow.\n1648:                             return;\n1649:                         }\n1650:                         // This is an edge case where we have a `move` closure\n1651:                         // inside a non-move closure, and the inner closure\n1652:                         // contains a mutation:\n1653:                         //\n1654:                         // let mut i = 0;\n1655:                         // || { move || { i += 1; }; };\n1656:                         //\n1657:                         // In this case our usual strategy of assuming that the\n1658:                         // variable will be captured by mutable reference is\n1659:                         // wrong, since `i` can be copied into the inner\n1660:                         // closure from a shared reference.\n1661:                         //\n1662:                         // As such we have to search for the local that this\n1663:                         // capture comes from and mark it as being used as mut.\n1664: \n1665:                         let Some(temp_mpi) = self.move_data.rev_lookup.find_local(local) else {\n1666:                             bug!(\"temporary should be tracked\");\n1667:                         };\n1668:                         let init = if let [init_index] = *self.move_data.init_path_map[temp_mpi] {\n1669:                             &self.move_data.inits[init_index]\n1670:                         } else {\n1671:                             bug!(\"temporary should be initialized exactly once\")\n1672:                         };\n1673: \n1674:                         let InitLocation::Statement(loc) = init.location else {\n1675:                             bug!(\"temporary initialized in arguments\")\n1676:                         };\n1677: \n1678:                         let body = self.body;\n1679:                         let bbd = &body[loc.block];\n1680:                         let stmt = &bbd.statements[loc.statement_index];\n1681:                         debug!(\"temporary assigned in: stmt={:?}\", stmt);\n1682: \n1683:                         match stmt.kind {\n1684:                             StatementKind::Assign(box (\n1685:                                 _,\n1686:                                 Rvalue::Ref(_, _, source)\n1687:                                 | Rvalue::Use(Operand::Copy(source) | Operand::Move(source)),\n1688:                             )) => {\n1689:                                 propagate_closure_used_mut_place(self, source);\n1690:                             }\n1691:                             _ => {\n1692:                                 bug!(\n1693:                                     \"closures should only capture user variables \\\n1694:                                  or references to user variables\"\n1695:                                 );\n1696:                             }\n1697:                         }\n1698:                     }\n1699:                     _ => propagate_closure_used_mut_place(self, place),\n1700:                 }\n1701:             }\n1702:             Operand::Constant(..) => {}\n1703:         }\n1704:     }\n1705: \n1706:     fn consume_operand(\n1707:         &mut self,\n1708:         location: Location,\n1709:         (operand, span): (&Operand<'tcx>, Span),\n1710:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1711:     ) {\n1712:         match *operand {\n1713:             Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1714:                 // copy of place: check if this is \"copy of frozen path\"\n1715:                 // (FIXME: see check_loans.rs)\n1716:                 self.access_place(\n1717:                     location,\n1718:                     (place, span),\n1719:                     (Deep, Read(ReadKind::Copy)),\n1720:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1721:                     state,\n1722:                 );\n1723: \n1724:                 // Finally, Operand::Constant(_) => {}\n1754:         }\n1755:     }\n1756: \n1757:     /// Checks whether a borrow of this place is invalidated when the function\n1758:     /// exits\n1759:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self))]\n1760:     fn check_for_invalidation_at_exit(\n1761:         &mut self,\n1762:         location: Location,\n1763:         borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\n1764:         span: Span,\n1765:     ) {\n1766:         let place = borrow.borrowed_place;\n1767:         let mut root_place = PlaceRef { local: place.local, projection: &[] };\n1768: \n1769:         // For now\n1770:         // we just know that all locals are dropped at function exit (otherwise\n1771:         // we'll have a memory leak) and assume that all statics have a destructor.\n1772: location,\n1801:                 borrow,\n1802:                 (place, span),\n1803:                 None,\n1804:             )\n1805:         }\n1806:     }\n1807: \n1808:     /// Reports an error if this is a borrow of local data.\n1809:     /// This is called for all Yield expressions on movable coroutines\n1810:     fn check_for_local_borrow(&mut self, borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>, yield_span: Span) {\n1811:         debug!(\"check_for_local_borrow({:?})\", borrow);\n1812: \n1813:         if borrow_of_local_data(borrow.borrowed_place) {\n1814:             let err = self.buffer_error(err);\n1820:         }\n1821:     }\n1822: \n1823:     fn check_activations(&mut self, location: Location, span: Span, state: &BorrowckDomain) {\n1824:         // Two-phase borrow support: For each activation that is newly\n1825:         // generated at this statement, check if it interferes with\n1826:         // another borrow.\n1827:         for &borrow_index in    assert!(match borrow.kind {\n1832:                 BorrowKind::Shared | BorrowKind::Fake(_) => false,\n1833:                 BorrowKind::Mut { .. } => true,\n1834:             });\n1835: \n1836: check_movable_place(&mut self, location: Location, place: Place<'tcx>) {\n1850:         use IllegalMoveOriginKind::*;\n1851: \n1852:         let body = self.body;\n1853:         let tcx =                     | ty::Pat(_, _)\n1882:                     | ty::Slice(_)\n1883:                     | ty::FnDef(_, _)\n1884:                     | ty::FnPtr(..)\n1885:                     | _)\n1894:                     | ty::Param(_)\n1895:                     | ty::Bound(_, _)\n1896:                     | ty::Infer(_)\n1897:                     | ty::Error(_)\n1898:                     | ty::Placeholder(_) => {\n1899:                         bug!(\"When Place is Deref it's type shouldn't be {place_ty:#?}\")\n1900:                     }\n1901:                 },\n1902: fn check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n1982:         &mut self,\n1983:         location: Location,\n1984:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n1985:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n1986:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1987:     ) {\n1988:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n1989: \n1990:         // Bad scenarios:\n1991:         //\n1992:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c`\n1993:         // 2. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c.d` (without first reinitializing `a.b.c.d`)\n1994:         // 3. Uninitialized `(a.b.c: &_)`, use of `*a.b.c`; note that with\n1995:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n1996:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n1997:         //\n1998:         // OK scenarios:\n1999:         //\n2000:         // 4. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2001:         // 5. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2002:         // 6. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2003:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2004:         // 7. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2005: \n2006:         // The dataflow tracks shallow prefixes distinctly (that is,\n2007:         // field-accesses on P distinctly from P itself), in order to\n2008:         // track substructure initialization separately from the whole\n2009:         // structure.\n2010:         //\n2011:         // E.g., when looking at (*a.b.c).d, if the closest prefix for\n2012:         // which we have a MovePath is `a.b`, then that means that the\n2013:         // initialization state of `a.b` is all we need to inspect to\n2014:         // know if `a.b.c` is valid (and from that we infer that the\n2015:         // dereference and `.d` access is also valid, since we assume\n2016:         // `a.b.c` is assigned a reference to an initialized and\n2017:         // well-formed record structure.)\n2018: \n2019:         // Therefore, if we seek out the *closest* prefix for which we\n2020:         // have a MovePath, that should capture the initialization\n2021:         // state for the place scenario.\n2022:         //\n2023:         // This code covers scenarios 1, 2, and 3.\n2024: \n2025:         debug!(\"check_if_full_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2026:         let (prefix, mpi) = self.move_path_closest_to(place_span.0);\n2027:         if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2028:             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2029:                 location,\n2030:                 desired_action,\n2031:                 (prefix, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2032:                 mpi,\n2033:             );\n2034:         } // Only query longest prefix with a MovePath, not further\n2035:         // ancestors; dataflow recurs on children when parents\n2036:         // move (to support partial (re)inits).\n2037:         //\n2038:         // (I.e., querying parents breaks scenario 7; but may want\n2039:         // to do such a query based on partial-init feature-gate.)\n2040:     }\n2041: \n2042:     /// Subslices correspond to multiple move paths, so we iterate through the\n2043:     /// elements of the base array. For each element we check\n2044:     ///\n2045:     /// * Does this element overlap with our slice.\n2046:     /// * Is any part of it uninitialized.\n2047:     fn check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2048:         &mut self,\n2049:         location: Location,\n2050:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2051:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2052:         maybe_uninits: &MixedBitSet<MovePathIndex>,\n2053:         from: u64,\n2054:         to: u64,\n2055:     ) {\n2056:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2057:             let move_paths = &self.move_data.move_paths;\n2058: \n2059:             let root_path = &move_paths[mpi];\n2060:             for (child_mpi, child_move_path) in root_path.children(move_paths) {\n2061:                 let last_proj = child_move_path.place.projection.last().unwrap();\n2062:                 if let ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, from_end, .. } = last_proj {\n2063:                     debug_assert!(!from_end, \"Array constant indexing shouldn't be `from_end`.\");\n2064: \n2065:                     if (from..to).contains(offset) {\n2066:                         let uninit_child =\n2067:                             self.move_data.find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(child_mpi, |mpi| {\n2068:                                 maybe_uninits.contains(mpi)\n2069:                             });\n2070: \n2071:                         if let Some(uninit_child) = uninit_child {\n2072:                             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2073:                                 location,\n2074:                                 desired_action,\n2075:                                 (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2076:                                 uninit_child,\n2077:                             );\n2078:                             return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2079:                         }\n2080:                     }\n2081:                 }\n2082:             }\n2083:         }\n2084:     }\n2085: \n2086:     fn check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2087:         &mut self,\n2088:         location: Location,\n2089:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2090:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2091:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2092:     ) {\n2093:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2094: \n2095:         // Bad scenarios:\n2096:         //\n2097:         // 1. All bad scenarios from `check_if_full_path_is_moved`\n2101:         //\n2102:         // OK scenarios:\n2103:         //\n2104:         // 3. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2105:         // 4. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2106:         // 5. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2107:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2108:         // 6. For example it will currently filter out\n2158:     /// places that are Copy; thus we do not track places of shared\n2159:     /// reference type. This routine will walk up a place along its\n2160:     /// prefixes, searching for a foundational place that *is*\n2161:     /// tracked in the MoveData.\n2162:     ///\n2163:     /// An Err result LookupResult::Parent(Some(mpi)) | LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => {\n2169:                 (self.move_data.move_paths[mpi].place.as_ref(), mpi)\n2170:             }\n2171:             LookupResult::Parent(None) => panic!(\"should have move path for every Local\"),\n2172:         }\n2173:     }\n2174: \n2175:     fn move_path_for_place(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> {}\n2249:                     }\n2250:                 }\n2251:             }\n2252:         }\n2253: \n2254:         fn check_parent_of_field<'a, 'tcx>(\n2255:             this: &mut ) {\n2261:             // rust-lang/rust#21232: Until Rust allows reads from the\n2262:             // initialized parts of partially initialized structs, we\n2263:             // will, starting with //\n2282:             // `let mut s = ...; drop(s.x); s.x=Val;`\n2283:             //\n2284:             // This does not use check_if_full_path_is_moved on\n2285:             // `base`, because that      );\n2306:                     shortest_uninit_seen = Some((prefix, mpi));\n2307:                 } else {\n2308:                     debug!(\"check_parent_of_field {:?} is definitely In this case, do not report an error here. There is an\n2315:                 // exception, if this is the first assignment into the union (that is, there is\n2316:                 // no move out from an earlier location) then this is an     fn check_access_permissions(\n2346:         &mut self,\n2347:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2348:         kind: ReadOrWrite,\n2349:         is_local_mutation_allowed: Err(place_err) => {\n2379:                         error_access = AccessKind::MutableBorrow;\n2380:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2381:                     }\n2382:                 }\n2383:             }\n2384:             Reservation(WriteKind::Mutate) | Write(WriteKind::Mutate) => {\n2385:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2386:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2387:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2388:                         return false;\n2389:                     }\n2390:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2391:                         error_access = AccessKind::Mutate;\n2392:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2393:                     }\n2394:                 }\n2395:             }\n2396: \n2397:             Reservation(\n2398:                 WriteKind::Move\n2399:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2400:                 |  span,\n2421:                         format!(\n2422:                             \"Accessing `{place:?}` with the kind `{kind:?}` shouldn't be possible\",\n2423:                         ),\n2424:                     );\n2425:                 }\n2426:                 return false;\n2427:             }\n2428:             Activation(..) => {\n2429:                 // permission checks are done at Reservation point.\n2430:                 return false;\n2431:             }\n2432:             Read(\n2433:                 ReadKind::Borrow(BorrowKind::Mut { .. } | BorrowKind::Shared | BorrowKind::Fake(_))\n2434:                 | ReadKind::Copy,\n2435:             ) => {\n2436:                 // Access authorized\n2437:                 return false;\n2438:             }\n2439:         }\n2440: \n2441:         // rust-lang/rust#21232, #54986: during period where we reject\n2442:         // partial initialization, do not complain about mutability\n2443:         // errors except ii.into_iter().find(|&&index| state.ever_inits.contains(index)).copied()\n2468:     }\n2469: \n2470:     /// Adds the place into the used mutable variables set\n2471:     fn add_used_mut(&mut self, These\\n153: /// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\\n154: /// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\\n155: ///\\n156: /// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\\n163: ///\\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\\n165: ///\\n166: /// ```text\\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\\n169: ///     'b,\\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \\\"closure kind\\\"\\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \\\"closure signature\\\"\\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\\n173: /// ]\\n174: /// ```\\n175: ///\\n176: /// We would \\\"renumber\\\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\\n177: ///\\n178: /// ```text\\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\\n181: ///     '2,\\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \\\"closure kind\\\"\\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \\\"closure signature\\\"\\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\\n185: /// ]\\n186: /// ```\\n187: ///\\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\\n191: /// outlives relationship.\\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01SSLZaSpuX2L8UexAFwJmPs","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - Type Checking - type_check** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/type_check/mod.rs:98): Performs type checking of the MIR body and generates region outlives constraints and liveness requirements.\\n\\n5. **Live Range Calculation - type_check/liveness** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/type_check/liveness/mod.rs): The generate function calls trace (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/type_check/liveness/trace.rs) which computes liveness information by backtracking through the CFG from uses to definitions, determining when each region is live at each location.\\n\\n6. **Borrow Set Construction - BorrowSet** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/borrow_set.rs:16): Gathers all borrows in the function and tracks their reservation and activation locations, particularly for two-phase borrows identified by BorrowData structures.\\n\\n7. **Place Conflict Detection - places_conflict** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/places_conflict.rs:81): Helper function that checks if two places conflict with a mutable borrow. The core analysis is in borrow_conflicts_with_place (line 104) which iterates through place projections in lockstep, using place_components_conflict to determine if projections are equal or disjoint at each step.\\n\\n8. **Two-Phase Borrow Resolution - check_activations** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs:1823): Checks two-phase borrow activations to ensure that activating a borrow doesn't conflict with existing borrows. Two-phase activation information is stored in TwoPhaseActivation enum in borrow_set.rs.\\n\\n9. **NLL Region Computation - compute_regions** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/nll.rs:113): Computes non-lexical lifetimes by creating a RegionInferenceContext, applying Polonius facts if enabled, and solving region constraints.\\n\\n10. **Region Inference Context** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/region_infer/mod.rs:79): Manages region inference with methods to propagate constraints and check type tests. Initialized with LoweredConstraints containing outlives constraints, type tests, and liveness constraints (LivenessValues from region_infer/values.rs).\\n\\n11. **Constraint Solving - solve** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/region_infer/mod.rs:493): Propagates outlives constraints through the region SCC graph, checks type tests for unsatisfiable constraints, and computes closure region requirements if needed.\\n\\n12. **Liveness Values Storage - LivenessValues** (compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/region_infer/values.rs:41): Stores the liveness information for regions, mapping from regions to the set of locations where they are live, used by the region inference engine to validate region constraints.\\n\\nThe analysis chain integrates MIR type checking, liveness analysis, place conflict detection, two-phase borrow handling, and constraint-based region inference to determine validity of borrows and compute required lifetime relationships.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
